# LLVM SelectionDAG Assertion Failure Diagnosis

## Your Task

A production build system using LLVM is crashing with the error: 'Cannot expand this type; LLVM lacks the right hooks'. Trace this assertion to its source in `llvm/llvm-project`. Find: 1. The C++ source file in `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/` that contains this error message or assertion. 2. The function in that file where the assertion fires (look for type legalization expansion logic). 3. The header file that defines the `EVT` (Extended Value Type) class and its `isSimple()` method (look in `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/`). 4. The file that defines the `LegalizeDAG` class which orchestrates type legalization and may call the expand function. Report the repo, file path, and function or class name for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

Perfect! I've completed the analysis of the LLVM SelectionDAG assertion failure and created the comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Files and Locations Identified:

1. **llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp** - Contains `ExpandIntegerResult` function (line 3024) where integer type expansion failures are reported with the error "Do not know how to expand the result of this operator!" (lines 3039-3040)

2. **llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp** - Contains `ExpandFloatResult` function with similar error handling for floating-point types (lines 1582-1583)

3. **llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/ValueTypes.h** - Defines the `EVT` (Extended Value Type) class (line 35) with the critical `isSimple()` method (lines 137-139) that checks if a type requires special handling

4. **llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeDAG.cpp** - Contains `SelectionDAGLegalize` class (line 88) that orchestrates operation legalization with `LegalizeOp` method (line 972)

5. **llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.h** - Defines `DAGTypeLegalizer` class (line 31) which is the core type legalization engine that coordinates expansion functions

The error occurs when the type legalization pass encounters a DAG node opcode that has no corresponding expansion handler. The framework checks if types are simple using `EVT::isSimple()`, and when expansion is required but unavailable, it reports the fatal error. This typically happens when custom hooks for type transformation haven't been provided by the target or when a node opcode is missing from the expansion switch statements.

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

Secondly, a new\\n45:   // node may be passed to the legalization core, but when analyzed may morph\\n46:   // into a different node, leaving the original node as a NewNode in the DAG.\\n47:   // A node may morph if one of its operands changes during analysis.  Whether\\n48:   // it actually morphs or not depends on whether, after updating its operands,\\n49:   // it is equivalent to an existing node: if so, it morphs into that existing\\n50:   // node (CSE). If a node morphs then the node it morphed into will\\n54:   // be used instead of it for legalization, however the original node continues\\n55:   // to live on in the DAG.\\n56:   // The conclusion is that though there may be nodes marked NewNode in the DAG,\\n57:   // all uses of such nodes are also marked NewNode: the result is a fungus of\\n58:   // NewNodes growing on top of the useful nodes, and perhaps using them, but\\n59:   // not used by them.\\n60: \\n61:   // If a value is mapped by ReplacedValues, then it must have no uses, except\\n62:   // by nodes marked NewNode (see above).\\n63: \\n64:   // The final node obtained by mapping by ReplacedValues is not marked NewNode.\\n65:   // Note that ReplacedValues should be applied iteratively.\\n66: \\n67:   // Note that the ReplacedValues map may also map deleted nodes (by iterating\\n68:   // over the DAG we never dereference deleted nodes).  This means that it may\\n69:   // also map nodes marked NewNode if the deallocated memory was reallocated as\\n70:   // another node, and that new node was not seen by the LegalizeTypes machinery\\n71:   // (for example because it was created but not used). Since this is rare,\n507:   // the code tries to minimize overhead in the non-morphing case.\n508: \n509:   std::vector<SDValue> NewOps;\n510:   unsigned NumProcessed = 0;\n511:   for (unsigned i = 0, e = N->getNumOperands(); i != e; ++i) {\n512:     SDValue OrigOp = N->getOperand(i);\n513:     SDValue Op = OrigOp;\n514: \n515:     AnalyzeNewValue(Op); // Op may morph.\n516: \n517:     if (Op.getNode()->getNodeId() == Processed)\n518:       ++NumProcessed;\n519: \n520:     if (!NewOps.empty()) {\n521:       // Some previous operand changed.  Add this one to the list.\n522:       NewOps.push_back(Op);\n523:     } else if (Op != OrigOp) {\n524:       // This is the first operand to change - add all operands so far.\n525:       llvm::append_range(NewOps, N->ops().take_front(i));\n526:       NewOps.push_back(Op);\n527:     }\n528:   }\n529: \n530:   // Some operands changed - update the node.\n531:   if (!NewOps.empty()) {\n532:     SDNode *M = DAG.UpdateNodeOperands(N, NewOps);\n533:     if (M != N) {\n534:       // The node morphed into a different node.  Normally for this to happen\n535:       // the original node would have to be marked NewNode.  However this can\n536:       // in theory momentarily not be the case while ReplaceValueWith is doing\n537:       // its stuff.  Mark the original node NewNode to help basic correctness\n538:       // checking.\n539:       N->setNodeId(NewNode);\n540:       if (M->getNodeId() != NewNode && M->getNodeId() != Unanalyzed)\n541:         // It morphed into a previously analyzed node - nothing more to do.\n542:         return M;\n543: \n544:       // It morphed into a different new node.  Do the equivalent of passing\n545:       // it to AnalyzeNewNode: expunge it and calculate the NodeId.  No need\n546:       // to remap the operands, since they are the same as the operands we\n547:       // remapped above.\n548:       N = M;\n549:     }\n550:   }\n551: ",

The enum has all the values.\\n37:   enum NodeIdFlags {\\n38:     /// All operands have been processed, so this node is ready to be handled.\\n39:     ReadyToProcess = 0,\\n40: \\n41:     /// This is a new node, not before seen, that was created in the process of\\n42:     /// legalizing some other node.\\n43:     NewNode = -1,\\n44: \\n45:     /// This node's ID needs to be set to the number of its unprocessed\\n46:     /// operands.\\n47:     Unanalyzed = -2,\\n48: \\n49:     /// This is a node that has already been processed.\\n50:     Processed = -3\\n51: \\n52:     // 1+ - This is a node which has this many unprocessed operands.\\n53:   };\\n54: private:\\n55: \\n56:   /// This is a bitvector that contains two bits for each simple value type,\\n57:   /// where the two bits correspond to the LegalizeAction enum from\\n58:   /// TargetLowering. This can be queried with \\\"getTypeAction(VT)\\\".\\n59:   TargetLowering::ValueTypeActionImpl ValueTypeActions;\\n60: \\n61:   /// Return how we should legalize values of this type.\\n62:   TargetLowering::LegalizeTypeAction getTypeAction(EVT VT) const {\\n63:     return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT);\\n64:   }\\n65: \\n66:   /// Return true if this type is legal on this target.\\n67:   bool isTypeLegal(EVT VT) const {\\n68:     return TLI.getTypeAction(*DAG.getContext(), VT) == TargetLowering::TypeLegal;\\n69:   }\\n70: \\n71:   /// Return true if this is a simple legal type.\\n72:   bool isSimpleLegalType(EVT VT) const {\\n73:     return VT.isSimple() && TLI.isTypeLegal(VT);\\n74:   }\\n75: \\n76:   EVT getSetCCResultType(EVT VT) const {\\n77:     return TLI.getSetCCResultType(DAG.getDataLayout(), *DAG.getContext(), VT);\\n78:   }\\n79: \\n80:   /// Pretend all of this node's results are legal.\\n81:   bool IgnoreNodeResults(SDNode *N) const {\\n82:     return N->getOpcode() == ISD::TargetConstant ||\\n83:            N->getOpcode() == ISD::Register;\\n84:   }\\n85: \\n86:   // Bijection from SDValue to unique id. As each created node gets a\\n87:   // new id we do not need to worry about reuse expunging.  Should we\\n88:   // run out of ids, we can do a one time expensive compactifcation.\\n89:   typedef unsigned TableId;\\n90: \\n91:   TableId NextValueId = 1;\\n92: \\n93:   SmallDenseMap<SDValue, TableId, 8> ValueToIdMap;\\n94:   SmallDenseMap<TableId, SDValue, 8> IdToValueMap;\\n95: \\n96:   /// For integer nodes that are below legal width, this map indicates what\\n97:   /// promoted value to use.\\n98:   SmallDenseMap<TableId, TableId, 8> PromotedIntegers;\\n99: \\n100:   /// For integer nodes that need to be expanded this map indicates which\\n101: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/llvm/llvm-project@0a9d7ffc037489d6047eff8052abdd35d025536c/-/blob/llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.h%3FL1-100\"}",

The production build system encounters this when attempting to expand a node type that has no handler. The actual error messages in the codebase report 'Do not know how to expand the result of this operator!' or 'Do not know how to expand this operator's operand!'\\n\\n**File Locations and Key Components:**\\n\\n1. **Primary Expansion Logic - llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeIntegerTypes.cpp**: Contains the ExpandIntegerResult function (starting at line 3024) which handles integer type expansion. The function implements a large switch statement to dispatch on operation types. When an unsupported operation is encountered (default case at line 3034), the code reports a fatal error at lines 3039-3040: 'Do not know how to expand the result of this operator!' Additionally, operand expansion errors are handled at line 5556.\\n\\n2. **Float Type Expansion - llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeFloatTypes.cpp**: Contains the ExpandFloatResult function which handles floating-point type expansion with identical error handling mechanisms. Float result expansion error occurs at lines 1582-1583, with operand expansion errors at line 2329.\\n\\n3. **EVT (Extended Value Type) Class - llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/ValueTypes.h**: Defines the EVT struct (line 35) which represents extended value types in the SelectionDAG. The critical isSimple() method is at line 137-139, which checks if VT.SimpleTy != MVT::INVALID_SIMPLE_VALUE_TYPE. This determines if a type is simple (can be handled by basic legalization) versus extended (requires special handling).\\n\\n4. **Operation Legalization Orchestrator - llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeDAG.cpp**: Contains the SelectionDAGLegalize class (line 88) which orchestrates the overall operation legalization process (distinct from type legalization). The LegalizeOp method (line 972) is the entry point for operation-level legalization.\\n\\n5. **Type Legalization Coordinator - llvm/lib/CodeGen/SelectionDAG/LegalizeTypes.h**: Defines the DAGTypeLegalizer class (line 31) which is the core type legalization engine. This class manages type transformation by coordinating between ExpandIntegerResult, ExpandFloatResult, and other expansion functions. It uses EVT::isSimple() to determine which types require special handling.\\n\\n**Error Chain:** When a DAG node has a type that needs expansion but no expansion handler is defined for that node's opcode, the type legalizer encounters the unsupported case in the switch statement. The framework calls report_fatal_error() with a diagnostic message. This happens when either (1) the target hasn't provided necessary legalization hooks through TargetLowering customization, or (2) a new operation type is used without corresponding expansion code.\"",

It coordinates between integer, float, and vector type expansion using functions like ExpandIntegerResult and ExpandFloatResult.\\n\\nThe error occurs in the type legalization phase when a DAG node with an unsupported type encounters no corresponding expansion handler. The framework checks if types are simple and legal using EVT::isSimple(), and when expansion is required but unavailable, it reports the fatal error. This typically happens when custom hooks for type transformation have not been provided by the target or when the node opcode is not in the expansion switch statements.\"",
